Services of this type cannot be added, removed,\n * or modified by applications.\n * The following attributes are automatically placed in each Provider object:\n * <table class=\"striped\">\n * <caption><b>Attributes Automatically Placed in a Provider Object</b></caption>\n * <thead>\n * <tr><th scope=\"col\">Name</th><th scope=\"col\">Value</th>\n * </thead>\n * <tbody style=\"text-align:left\">\n * <tr><th scope=\"row\">{@code Provider.id name}</th>\n *     <td>{@code String.valueOf(provider.getName())}</td>\n * <tr><th scope=\"row\">{@code Provider.id version}</th>\n *     <td>{@code String.valueOf(provider.getVersionStr())}</td>\n * <tr><th scope=\"row\">{@code Provider.id info}</th>\n *     <td>{@code String.valueOf(provider.getInfo())}</td>\n * <tr><th scope=\"row\">{@code Provider.id className}</th>\n *     <td>{@code provider.getClass().getName()}</td>\n * </tbody>\n * </table>\n *\n * <p>Each provider has a name and a version string. A provider normally\n * identifies itself with a file named {@code java.security.Provider}\n * in the resource directory {@code META-INF/services}.\n * Security providers are looked up via the {@link ServiceLoader} mechanism\n * using the {@link ClassLoader#getSystemClassLoader application class loader}.\n *\n * <p>Providers may be configured such that they are automatically\n * installed and made available at runtime via the\n * {@link Security#getProviders() Security.getProviders()} method.\n * The mechanism for configuring and installing security providers is\n * implementation-specific.\n *\n * @implNote\n * The JDK implementation supports static registration of the security","numLines":100,"startLine":1,"totalLines":2015}}}

comprehensive set of interconnected classes and configuration files:\\n\\n## Core Framework Components\\n\\n**Base Provider Class (java/security/Provider.java)**: The fundamental abstract class that all security providers extend. It provides the putService() method (line 1221) used to register cryptographic algorithms and other security services. The Service inner class (line 1500) encapsulates individual service implementations with metadata like type, algorithm name, class name, and aliases.\\n\\n**Security Class (java/security/Security.java)**: The public API entry point for managing security providers, allowing applications to get providers, search for services, and manage the provider list.\\n\\n## Lazy-Loading Mechanism\\n\\n**ProviderConfig (sun/security/jca/ProviderConfig.java)**: The lazy-loading mechanism that maps provider names to their implementation classes. It implements caching and retry logic (MAX_LOAD_TRIES = 30) to efficiently load providers on-demand rather than eagerly at startup. Provider classes can be either ServiceLoader-based (module names) or classpath-based (legacy class names).\\n\\n**ProviderList (sun/security/jca/ProviderList.java)**: Manages the ordered collection of configured providers. It uses ProviderConfig instances and lazy-loads providers during service lookup. Initialized from security properties via fromSecurityProperties() (line 88), it uses ServiceLoader to discover module-based providers and handles the EMPTY_PROVIDER placeholder during initialization to avoid circular dependencies.\\n\\n**Providers (sun/security/jca/Providers.java)**: The registry that maintains system-wide and thread-local provider lists. It initializes from security.properties configuration (line 55) and includes special handling for JAR verification with a hardcoded list of providers (SUN, SunRsaSign, SunEC, SunJCE - lines 85-92).\\n\\n## Cryptographic Provider Implementations\\n\\n**SunJCE Provider (com/sun/crypto/provider/SunJCE.java)**: Implements cryptographic algorithms including AES, DES, Triple DES, Blowfish, ARCFOUR, RC2, PBE, Diffie-Hellman key agreement, HMAC, ChaCha20, DHKEM, and ML-KEM. Uses the ps() helper methods (lines 107-122) to call putService() for algorithm registration.\\n\\n**SunJSSE Provider (sun/security/ssl/SunJSSE.java)**: Implements SSL/TLS and DTLS support. Registers KeyManagerFactory, TrustManagerFactory, SSLContext (with versions TLSv1, TLSv1.1, TLSv1.2, TLSv1.3, DTLSv1.0, DTLSv1.2), and PKCS12 KeyStore services. Uses the ps() helper method (lines 49-52) for putService() calls.\\n\\n**SunEC Provider (sun/security/ec/SunEC.java)**: Provides elliptic curve cryptography support including ECDSA signatures with various SHA-2 and SHA-3 variants, elliptic curve key factories, key pair generation, and algorithm parameters. Uses custom ProviderService and ProviderServiceA inner classes (lines 58-67) that extend Provider.Service with specialized newInstance() logic for dynamic instantiation.\\n\\n**Sun Provider (sun/security/provider/Sun.java)**: Implements core algorithms including DSA key/parameter generation, DSA signing, SHA-1 and MD5 digests, SecureRandom, X.509 certificates, PKCS12/JKS/DKS keystores, PKIX CertPath validation/building, and certificate stores. Uses SunEntries (line 55) to generate its service list.\\n\\n**SunRsaSign Provider (sun/security/rsa/SunRsaSign.java)**: Provides RSA signature algorithms, RSA key factory, and RSA key pair generation. Similar to Sun, it uses SunRsaSignEntries (line 50) for service registration.\\n\\n## Service Registry Helpers\\n\\n**SunEntries (sun/security/provider/SunEntries.java)**: Iterator-based service builder for the Sun provider. Dynamically creates Provider.Service instances based on platform availability (e.g., NativePRNG variants), and registers signature algorithms (SHA*withDSA), MessageDigest (SHA-1, SHA-2, SHA-3, MD5), KeyFactory (DSA, X.509), CertFactory, CertStore, and other security services.\\n\\n**SunRsaSignEntries (sun/security/rsa/SunRsaSignEntries.java)**: Iterator-based service builder for the SunRsaSign provider, similarly registering RSA-related cryptographic services.\\n\\n**VerificationProvider (sun/security/provider/VerificationProvider.java)**: A fallback provider used only when Sun and SunRsaSign main classes have been removed, providing the same algorithms for JAR verification resilience.\\n\\n## Service Discovery Framework\\n\\n**GetInstance (sun/security/jca/GetInstance.java)**: Utility class providing static methods to retrieve Provider.Service instances from the provider list by type and algorithm name. Delegates to ProviderList for the actual service lookup (lines 64-73).\\n\\n**ServiceId (sun/security/jca/ServiceId.java)**: Identifies a unique service through provider name, service type, and algorithm name.\\n\\n**JCAUtil (sun/security/jca/JCAUtil.java)**: Additional utility methods for JCA framework operations.\\n\\n## Configuration\\n\\n**java.security Properties File (java.base/share/conf/security/java.security)**: Static provider configuration declaring the default provider order (lines 96-100): SUN, SunRsaSign, SunEC, SunJSSE, and SunJCE. Uses the 'security.provider.tbd=<provName>' format for ServiceLoader-based discovery, where providers are loaded by their module name (e.g., 'SUN' loads sun.security.provider.Sun).\\n\\n## Registration Flow\\n\\nThe framework follows this initialization chain:\\n1. Security class initialization loads java.security properties\\n2. Providers.fromSecurityProperties() → ProviderList.fromSecurityProperties()\\n3. ProviderList creates ProviderConfig instances for each configured provider\\n4. On first service lookup, ProviderConfig.getProvider() lazy-loads the provider class\\n5. Provider constructor calls putService() for each registered service\\n6. GetInstance retrieves services from ProviderList when applications request algorithms\\n\\nThis design provides: (1) Lazy initialization for reduced startup time, (2) Modular architecture supporting dynamic providers, (3) Backward compatibility with both ServiceLoader and classpath-based loading, and (4) Efficient service lookup with caching.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":216,"cache_read_input_tokens":51656,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":216},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"78147fca-237e-4d20-8db8-e97b4c08ca92","uuid":"e3e20c2b-9bb2-4fde-aea9-7fac9780e938"}

Initialized from security properties via fromSecurityProperties() (line 88), it uses ServiceLoader to discover module-based providers and handles the EMPTY_PROVIDER placeholder during initialization to avoid circular dependencies.\\n\\n**Providers (sun/security/jca/Providers.java)**: The registry that maintains system-wide and thread-local provider lists. It initializes from security.properties configuration (line 55) and includes special handling for JAR verification with a hardcoded list of providers (SUN, SunRsaSign, SunEC, SunJCE - lines 85-92).\\n\\n## Cryptographic Provider Implementations\\n\\n**SunJCE Provider (com/sun/crypto/provider/SunJCE.java)**: Implements cryptographic algorithms including AES, DES, Triple DES, Blowfish, ARCFOUR, RC2, PBE, Diffie-Hellman key agreement, HMAC, ChaCha20, DHKEM, and ML-KEM. Uses the ps() helper methods (lines 107-122) to call putService() for algorithm registration.\\n\\n**SunJSSE Provider (sun/security/ssl/SunJSSE.java)**: Implements SSL/TLS and DTLS support. Registers KeyManagerFactory, TrustManagerFactory, SSLContext (with versions TLSv1, TLSv1.1, TLSv1.2, TLSv1.3, DTLSv1.0, DTLSv1.2), and PKCS12 KeyStore services. Uses the ps() helper method (lines 49-52) for putService() calls.\\n\\n**SunEC Provider (sun/security/ec/SunEC.java)**: Provides elliptic curve cryptography support including ECDSA signatures with various SHA-2 and SHA-3 variants, elliptic curve key factories, key pair generation, and algorithm parameters. Uses custom ProviderService and ProviderServiceA inner classes (lines 58-67) that extend Provider.Service with specialized newInstance() logic for dynamic instantiation.\\n\\n**Sun Provider (sun/security/provider/Sun.java)**: Implements core algorithms including DSA key/parameter generation, DSA signing, SHA-1 and MD5 digests, SecureRandom, X.509 certificates, PKCS12/JKS/DKS keystores, PKIX CertPath validation/building, and certificate stores. Uses SunEntries (line 55) to generate its service list.\\n\\n**SunRsaSign Provider (sun/security/rsa/SunRsaSign.java)**: Provides RSA signature algorithms, RSA key factory, and RSA key pair generation. Similar to Sun, it uses SunRsaSignEntries (line 50) for service registration.\\n\\n## Service Registry Helpers\\n\\n**SunEntries (sun/security/provider/SunEntries.java)**: Iterator-based service builder for the Sun provider. Dynamically creates Provider.Service instances based on platform availability (e.g., NativePRNG variants), and registers signature algorithms (SHA*withDSA), MessageDigest (SHA-1, SHA-2, SHA-3, MD5), KeyFactory (DSA, X.509), CertFactory, CertStore, and other security services.\\n\\n**SunRsaSignEntries (sun/security/rsa/SunRsaSignEntries.java)**: Iterator-based service builder for the SunRsaSign provider, similarly registering RSA-related cryptographic services.\\n\\n**VerificationProvider (sun/security/provider/VerificationProvider.java)**: A fallback provider used only when Sun and SunRsaSign main classes have been removed, providing the same algorithms for JAR verification resilience.\\n\\n## Service Discovery Framework\\n\\n**GetInstance (sun/security/jca/GetInstance.java)**: Utility class providing static methods to retrieve Provider.Service instances from the provider list by type and algorithm name. Delegates to ProviderList for the actual service lookup (lines 64-73).\\n\\n**ServiceId (sun/security/jca/ServiceId.java)**: Identifies a unique service through provider name, service type, and algorithm name.\\n\\n**JCAUtil (sun/security/jca/JCAUtil.java)**: Additional utility methods for JCA framework operations.\\n\\n## Configuration\\n\\n**java.security Properties File (java.base/share/conf/security/java.security)**: Static provider configuration declaring the default provider order (lines 96-100): SUN, SunRsaSign, SunEC, SunJSSE, and SunJCE. Uses the 'security.provider.tbd=<provName>' format for ServiceLoader-based discovery, where providers are loaded by their module name (e.g., 'SUN' loads sun.security.provider.Sun).\\n\\n## Registration Flow\\n\\nThe framework follows this initialization chain:\\n1. Security class initialization loads java.security properties\\n2. Providers.fromSecurityProperties() → ProviderList.fromSecurityProperties()\\n3. ProviderList creates ProviderConfig instances for each configured provider\\n4. On first service lookup, ProviderConfig.getProvider() lazy-loads the provider class\\n5. Provider constructor calls putService() for each registered service\\n6. GetInstance retrieves services from ProviderList when applications request algorithms\\n\\nThis design provides: (1) Lazy initialization for reduced startup time, (2) Modular architecture supporting dynamic providers, (3) Backward compatibility with both ServiceLoader and classpath-based loading, and (4) Efficient service lookup with caching.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

Initialized from security properties via fromSecurityProperties() (line 88), it uses ServiceLoader to discover module-based providers and handles the EMPTY_PROVIDER placeholder during initialization to avoid circular dependencies.\\n\\n**Providers (sun/security/jca/Providers.java)**: The registry that maintains system-wide and thread-local provider lists. It initializes from security.properties configuration (line 55) and includes special handling for JAR verification with a hardcoded list of providers (SUN, SunRsaSign, SunEC, SunJCE - lines 85-92).\\n\\n## Cryptographic Provider Implementations\\n\\n**SunJCE Provider (com/sun/crypto/provider/SunJCE.java)**: Implements cryptographic algorithms including AES, DES, Triple DES, Blowfish, ARCFOUR, RC2, PBE, Diffie-Hellman key agreement, HMAC, ChaCha20, DHKEM, and ML-KEM. Uses the ps() helper methods (lines 107-122) to call putService() for algorithm registration.\\n\\n**SunJSSE Provider (sun/security/ssl/SunJSSE.java)**: Implements SSL/TLS and DTLS support. Registers KeyManagerFactory, TrustManagerFactory, SSLContext (with versions TLSv1, TLSv1.1, TLSv1.2, TLSv1.3, DTLSv1.0, DTLSv1.2), and PKCS12 KeyStore services. Uses the ps() helper method (lines 49-52) for putService() calls.\\n\\n**SunEC Provider (sun/security/ec/SunEC.java)**: Provides elliptic curve cryptography support including ECDSA signatures with various SHA-2 and SHA-3 variants, elliptic curve key factories, key pair generation, and algorithm parameters. Uses custom ProviderService and ProviderServiceA inner classes (lines 58-67) that extend Provider.Service with specialized newInstance() logic for dynamic instantiation.\\n\\n**Sun Provider (sun/security/provider/Sun.java)**: Implements core algorithms including DSA key/parameter generation, DSA signing, SHA-1 and MD5 digests, SecureRandom, X.509 certificates, PKCS12/JKS/DKS keystores, PKIX CertPath validation/building, and certificate stores. Uses SunEntries (line 55) to generate its service list.\\n\\n**SunRsaSign Provider (sun/security/rsa/SunRsaSign.java)**: Provides RSA signature algorithms, RSA key factory, and RSA key pair generation. Similar to Sun, it uses SunRsaSignEntries (line 50) for service registration.\\n\\n## Service Registry Helpers\\n\\n**SunEntries (sun/security/provider/SunEntries.java)**: Iterator-based service builder for the Sun provider. Dynamically creates Provider.Service instances based on platform availability (e.g., NativePRNG variants), and registers signature algorithms (SHA*withDSA), MessageDigest (SHA-1, SHA-2, SHA-3, MD5), KeyFactory (DSA, X.509), CertFactory, CertStore, and other security services.\\n\\n**SunRsaSignEntries (sun/security/rsa/SunRsaSignEntries.java)**: Iterator-based service builder for the SunRsaSign provider, similarly registering RSA-related cryptographic services.\\n\\n**VerificationProvider (sun/security/provider/VerificationProvider.java)**: A fallback provider used only when Sun and SunRsaSign main classes have been removed, providing the same algorithms for JAR verification resilience.\\n\\n## Service Discovery Framework\\n\\n**GetInstance (sun/security/jca/GetInstance.java)**: Utility class providing static methods to retrieve Provider.Service instances from the provider list by type and algorithm name. Delegates to ProviderList for the actual service lookup (lines 64-73).\\n\\n**ServiceId (sun/security/jca/ServiceId.java)**: Identifies a unique service through provider name, service type, and algorithm name.\\n\\n**JCAUtil (sun/security/jca/JCAUtil.java)**: Additional utility methods for JCA framework operations.\\n\\n## Configuration\\n\\n**java.security Properties File (java.base/share/conf/security/java.security)**: Static provider configuration declaring the default provider order (lines 96-100): SUN, SunRsaSign, SunEC, SunJSSE, and SunJCE. Uses the 'security.provider.tbd=<provName>' format for ServiceLoader-based discovery, where providers are loaded by their module name (e.g., 'SUN' loads sun.security.provider.Sun).\\n\\n## Registration Flow\\n\\nThe framework follows this initialization chain:\\n1. Security class initialization loads java.security properties\\n2. Providers.fromSecurityProperties() → ProviderList.fromSecurityProperties()\\n3. ProviderList creates ProviderConfig instances for each configured provider\\n4. On first service lookup, ProviderConfig.getProvider() lazy-loads the provider class\\n5. Provider constructor calls putService() for each registered service\\n6. GetInstance retrieves services from ProviderList when applications request algorithms\\n\\nThis design provides: (1) Lazy initialization for reduced startup time, (2) Modular architecture supporting dynamic providers, (3) Backward compatibility with both ServiceLoader and classpath-based loading, and (4) Efficient service lookup with caching.\"\n}\n","numLines":48,"startLine":1,"totalLines":48}}}
